  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6102403d-b791-4bb6-b153-b516dc92f44f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText15289867670361441679" style="display:none">Sophie Foster is on the run—but at least she's not alone.<br /><br />Her closest friends from the Lost Cities have gone with her to join the Black Swan. They still have doubts about the shadowy organization, but the only way to find answers is to start working with them. And as they settle into their new lives, they uncover secrets far bigger than anything they’d imagined.<br /><br />But their enemies are far from done, and unleash a terrifying plague that threatens the safety of an entire species. Sophie and her friends fight with everything they have—with new allies joining them—but every choice has consequences. And trusting the wrong person could prove deadly.<br /><br />In this game-changing fourth book in the Keeper of the Lost Cities series, Sophie must question everything to find a truth that will either save her world—or shatter it.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Actually I dont get why we're all talking bad about other characters,i think they're all great...Im Team Keefianafitzster....how do we add Dex into th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Actually I dont get why we're all talking bad about other characters,i think they're all great...Im Team Keefianafitzster....how do we add Dex into the mix? Lol<br />I was supporting Team Fitz since book one,but book two made me fall a little more towards Keefe...and book three,back to Fitz,BUT..<br />When alot of people say they kinda semi-hate Dex,i dont feel so...he never meant to do that,plus he was feeling left out and a little jealous towards Sophie n Fitz's connection,plusss Keefe often helped her out in missions and that leaves Dex,so when he thought he could prove he was useful..it all backfired,and he really regretted it,right? And NOT TO MENTION who exactly was the one to save Sophie from Everblaze and Brant? Yea and who exactly was the one to willingly risk him n his family sent to EXILE just to get rid of the you-know-what?<br />So i demand a truce...Let's not fall to deeply into our 'team' enough to point out the others' faults and all that,yea?<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1009436706" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5219913692855504441">WOO HOO--I can finally reveal the title! <br/><br/>AND NOW WE HAVE A COVER!!!!!!!!<br/><br/>And now my editor has officially approved the draft!!!! I know that probably doesn't sound like that groundbreaking of news, but it's huge because it means the book is *almost* done. Just needs a few more polish rounds and it'll be ready to go in November. So I'm moving the book to my "read" shelf to celebrate (even though I've probably read it 300 times already, no joke) :)<br/><br/>(And in case you can't tell, that's Sophie, Keefe, </span>
  <span id="freeText5219913692855504441" style="display:none">WOO HOO--I can finally reveal the title! <br /><br />AND NOW WE HAVE A COVER!!!!!!!!<br /><br />And now my editor has officially approved the draft!!!! I know that probably doesn't sound like that groundbreaking of news, but it's huge because it means the book is *almost* done. Just needs a few more polish rounds and it'll be ready to go in November. So I'm moving the book to my "read" shelf to celebrate (even though I've probably read it 300 times already, no joke) :)<br /><br />(And in case you can't tell, that's Sophie, Keefe, and Biana on the cover--but don't worry, the other boys are in the book just as much!)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5219913692855504441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11659724754336537291">Holy angst! So enjoyable! I seem to be unable to stop raving about this series. It's seriously addictive!<br/><br/>⛓SPOILER ALERT!⛓ <br/>I love stories about crazy schools, it's my pet topic and Exillium is so very seriously bonkers that one can't help loving this part of the plot. THIS school offers some serious fun and entertainment to attendees (I'm kidding!). <br/><br/>✨ Its attendees are called Waywards (while in Foxfire they are called Prodigies!). <br/>✨ Waywards are not allowed to use names or interact with each othe</span>
  <span id="freeText11659724754336537291" style="display:none">Holy angst! So enjoyable! I seem to be unable to stop raving about this series. It's seriously addictive!<br /><br />⛓SPOILER ALERT!⛓ <br />I love stories about crazy schools, it's my pet topic and Exillium is so very seriously bonkers that one can't help loving this part of the plot. THIS school offers some serious fun and entertainment to attendees (I'm kidding!). <br /><br />✨ Its attendees are called Waywards (while in Foxfire they are called Prodigies!). <br />✨ Waywards are not allowed to use names or interact with each other. <br />✨ They are welcomed into school by surprise, hanging upside down! And the very botched procedure of Waywards getting out of this predicament helps teachers to sort them into an even more botched system Hemisphere-oriented groups (Right, Left or Ambi). <br />✨ The curriculum of Exillium doesn't sound as bad as might be reasonably expected from the info above. It actually might be more useful than Foxfire, since it focuses on skills not talents. Including slowing breath (Dex is good at it already, as we know!), blinking control, developing night vision, regulating body temperature, hunger suppression, levitation and telekinesis. <br />✨ Exillium's location changes every day and is always in the Neutral Territories. <br />✨ The fashion sense in Exillium? Don't get me started on it!<br />✨ You don't get expelled from here: you get EJECTED!<br />✨ The economic situation with it, incl. the supplies and pretty much everything else is horrible and makes initially little sense in the light of how everything is supposed to be economically effortless for the elves who get all those fun endowment funds. I'm not spoiling this at the moment. Suffice it to say that there is a lot more to this all!<br /><br />Who knew kids' books could be THIS MUCH FUN?<br /><br />Q:<br />I will do everything in my power to help my world. Their instincts know that if they did, they would shelter the younglings and weaken their ability to survive. (c)<br />Q:<br />I do my best thinking when I can tuck my consciousness away. Every time Fitz spews up black gunk, it makes Biana barf, and then Della loses it—and repeat! (c)<br />Q:<br />Yeah, I’m cute and glittery—what’s it to you? (c)<br />Q:<br />“I guess everyone has a few crazy family members they’d don’t know what to do with. You’ll be mine.” (c)<br />Q:<br />LEAVE IT TO you to try to burn down Exillium on the first day (c)<br />Q:<br />All I know is it tasted like kissing a muskog.”<br />“And you have a lot of experience with that?” (c)<br />Q:<br />“I listened. And I realized their voices had been silenced. So I gave them mine. I sang of sunlight and rain and rich soil. And hope.               <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2899169250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6228743811992699033">4.5 stars<br/><br/>This would have been a 3.5 star read because it took half of book to get me re-engaged, but then THAT ENDING sequence. <br/><br/><b>Pacing:</b> ★★★<br/><b>Plot development:</b> ★★★★★<br/><b>Character development:</b> ★★★★★ for Keefe, ★★★ for everyone else.<br/><br/><i>Neverseen</i> is the fourth installment in the Keeper of the Lost Cities series and arguably the slowest of the first four. Sophie and her group of friends have been banished from the Lost Cities/elven society, and are on the run with members of the rebel organization, the Black </span>
  <span id="freeText6228743811992699033" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />This would have been a 3.5 star read because it took half of book to get me re-engaged, but then THAT ENDING sequence. <br /><br /><b>Pacing:</b> ★★★<br /><b>Plot development:</b> ★★★★★<br /><b>Character development:</b> ★★★★★ for Keefe, ★★★ for everyone else.<br /><br /><i>Neverseen</i> is the fourth installment in the Keeper of the Lost Cities series and arguably the slowest of the first four. Sophie and her group of friends have been banished from the Lost Cities/elven society, and are on the run with members of the rebel organization, the Black Swan. <br /><br /><b>For a novel that was "on the run," we spent a fair amount of time enjoying ourselves in an underground grotto in a tree house and interpersonal drama</b>. Don't get me wrong, the dialogue and relationships remained interesting and the setting was cool, but <b>it was S L O W</b>.<br /><br />Given its snail-like pacing for the majority of the novel—and the fact that it's a whopping 700 pages—<b>I found myself setting it down way more than I did for the first three</b>. However, once the story kicked off and Sophie's team makes some disturbing discoveries about a plague that's threatening the gnomes and a plot bubbling in the ogre's land, <i>Neverseen</i> really kicks off. <br /><br />Oh, and Keefe. My poor, precious snowflake. He wrenched my heart right out at the end there, but there appears to be hope at the end of the tunnel. (At least, there BETTER BE. Lol.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6228743811992699033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2956920382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2956920382" />
    <a title="BrooKe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke"><img alt="BrooKe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583732525p2/87485390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2956920382?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BrooKe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BrooKe" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke">BrooKe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2956920382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8310454747102263566">4.5/5 | I want to scream, cry, rage and throw things all at once. Since I have been warned not to do any of those things, here’s an attempt at gathering my <b>totally calm thoughts</b>.<br/><br/>Before I get started, allow me to explain how it is times like this that I wish I was a more renown book reviewer so that I could preach my adoration for this relatively underrated series to a larger audience and help it gain the notoriety it truly deserves. <br/><br/>*sigh* <i>I'll get there.</i><br/><br/><br/><b>P L O T</b><br/><br/>This was the weak point (and I use</span>
  <span id="freeText8310454747102263566" style="display:none">4.5/5 | I want to scream, cry, rage and throw things all at once. Since I have been warned not to do any of those things, here’s an attempt at gathering my <b>totally calm thoughts</b>.<br /><br />Before I get started, allow me to explain how it is times like this that I wish I was a more renown book reviewer so that I could preach my adoration for this relatively underrated series to a larger audience and help it gain the notoriety it truly deserves. <br /><br />*sigh* <i>I'll get there.</i><br /><br /><br /><b>P L O T</b><br /><br />This was the weak point (and I use weak in a very loose sense seeing as just about everything about this book was far from weak, I assure you). <br /><br />I wish the adventures in Italy lasted longer because they were really fun! Seeing Sophie’s elvin buddies trying to blend in with humans was a comedy goldmine—from girls gawking at Fitz to Keefe discovering ice cream and Batman. I NEED them to spend more time in the human world! No, <i>I do not care</i> that the elves call them ‘the Forbidden Cities’ for a reason. <br /><br />Sadly, majority of the book was spent in Alluveterre, which was kind of dull. All portions of the plot spent there were essentially one <b>long</b> training montage mostly focused on Sophie and Fitz’s outrageously quirky bestie bond. Not exciting stuff, I must admit. <br /><br />I was in it more for the characters because, while we may have been suspended in one exceedingly drab setting over most of the course of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22733616.Neverseen__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___4_" title="Neverseen (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #4) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Neverseen</a>, I was off on a rollercoaster of character emotions so the setting didn’t bother me that much in the end.<br /><br />HOWEVER, things got a little more spicy once reaching the dreaded Exillium! I much preferred that place to even Foxfire! It has to be revisited! It was not interchangeable for anywhere without the Council like Alluveterre was but was rather defined, captivating and so, so magical.<br /><br />I cannot go into the few interesting plot developments because DUH SPOILERS! I will say, though, that it kind of sucks that I got spoiled about most of the twists (<i>curse you, Pinterest, and my incessant craving to look up Keeper of the Lost Cities fan art!</i>). I’m still a mess, but I would have been an utter <b>WRECK</b> if I hadn’t known said twists were coming! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5265998.Shannon_Messenger" title="Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Shannon Messenger</a> sure knows how to deliver proper, brutal shock value.<br /><br /><br /><b>C H A R A C T E R S</b><br /><br />Sophie who? Fuck that; I’m starting with <b>Keefe</b>! <br /><br />Keefe. Keefe, Keefe, <b>Keefe</b>. Keefe Sencen. Keefe Sencen, Keefe, <i>Keefe</i>, <b>Keefe Sencen</b>. Why am I crying by just typing his name out several times? <br /><br />Seriously. <b>I could write poetry about this dude.</b><br /><br />I just... my heart is shattered. He goes through such a range of believable, truly conceivable emotions and that is what hurts most of all. It all feels so fucking <i>REAL</i>. Going into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842828.Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___1_" title="Keeper of the Lost Cities (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #1) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Keeper of the Lost Cities</a>, getting such a raw but somehow complex character out of the series was absolutely unfathomable to me. I could not have begun to guess at Keefe Sencen’s emotional journey and the fact that <b>I am quite literally getting pretty damn emotional by just vaguely glossing over it, several days after finishing Neverseen,</b> just goes to show how impactful his storyline is. And I have to praise Shannon Messenger’s writing here because it is one thing to have a brilliant character concept (as Keefe does) but it is quite another to execute it in such a sense where it is this ridiculously hard-hitting.<br /><br />Keefe legitimately made the book for me. Without him, I honestly think this book would have been a 3 star read. Then again, I can’t even imagine this series without him.<br /><br />(Gods, if I keep at this high as hell praise for this character every Keeper review, I am going to run out of coherent things to say.)<br /><br />So Sophie. I love Sophie. While she may be a “Special Sophieflake”, as her ingenious human classmates put it (and I truly appreciate the self awareness there, Shannon XP), my List of Things Sophie Gets That No One Else Does Because She’s Special is SO MUCH SHORTER! It goes as follows:<br />Sophie can follow someone’s thoughts to their source, Sophie can age 9 months in a day, Sophie has 1711101927378911 powers.<br /><br />But that’s it. I consider this <i>massive progress.</i><br /><br />In all seriousness, I can’t not adore her. She is so down to earth, so supportive, so selfless and just and grounded. Everything she does for all of her friends—especially Keefe—is just... so admirable. She is a truly lovable protagonist, even more so in a supporting role. <br /><br />Fitz Vacker. <b>The Gryffindor of Gryffindors</b>. The Gryffindoriest of them all. I really don’t know what else to say. I’m trying to like him, I really am, but he’s so <i>booooooooringgg</i>. I know he’s got it in him! Just because Pyrokinetics are forbidden don’t mean Shannon gotta forbid Fitz from showing his own lil’ fire! <br /><br />It’s official: Biana takes the title of most boring Vacker. That is quite an achievement considering her competition. The only remotely interesting Vacker is Alden and he just so happens to be the only member of the family that isn’t present in Neverseen.<br /><br />I am impressed and frankly thrilled that Dex is still in the picture. If anything, I’m surprised! I really like him. I think it says a lot about Dex that he takes the time to learn underrated skills like advanced thermoregulation and holding your breath for extended periods of time. He’s genuinely really clever and works for his abilities rather than just having them handed over to him (<b>cough</b> <i>Sophie</i> <b>cough cough</b>). No shade. <br /><br />The second most prominent source of my excitement: Tam and Linh. They have a fascinating backstory, really defined characteristics and AMAZING powers. Describing Linh as a fragile bird while her brother, Tam, is the prowling tiger is a perfect encapsulation of their characters and paints a striking contrast. These two could bring so much to the table!<br /><br />Their look may just be the best thing about them because, first of all: Hello there, Representation! I was wondering where you went off to for a second! Of course, combined with their silvery-black-hair-twin-dynamic-anime-character-Kpop-star look, it’s a recipe for greatness!<br /><br /><br /><b>R E L A T I O N S H I P S</b><br /><br />So instead of a girl choosing between zoophilia and necrophilia (in infamous <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> fashion), we have the sweet love story of an adorable Hufflepuff breaking the hearts of millions of loyal readers (such as myself) by being into a Gryffindor and also a Slytherin. There is no Ravenclaw in the equation as their logical mind would be able to deduce in an instant that <b>the Slytherin is the obvious choice</b>.<br /><br />Okay. No more stalling. This is <i>serious</i>. Let’s get to Sokeefe. <br /><br />Sophie. And. Keefe. Are. O. T. P. The amount of moments they have in this book is <b>fucking unreal</b> and I <b>cannot</b> begin to comprehend <b>how</b>, exactly, one does not ship them. <br /><br /><i>“The sharpness in his tone made Sophie reach for his hand.<br />“I’m fine,” he promised. But he didn’t pull away.”</i><br /><br />Keefe and Sophie ARE SO FUCKING CUTE. MY HEART <b>MELTED</b> WHEN HE WAS GRIEVING AND SHE WAS GOING OUT OF HER WAY TO MAKE HIM FEEL BETTER, IGNORING EVERYONE’S WARNINGS TO KEEP HER DISTANCE. SHE KEPT HER DISTANCE WHEN FITZ AND BIANA WERE GRIEVING IN BOOK 2 BUT <b>SHE <i>REFUSED</i> TO LEAVE KEEFE ALONE</b>. This girl treasures Keefe’s smiles and laughs and, Jesus Christ almighty, I <i>completely</i> understand why Keefe would have a thing for her. She’s the one that cheers him up but is also his shoulder to cry on.<br /><br />They are <i>made</i> of comfort and loyalty. There is so much of it here and, once again, it hurts my heart because, on one hand, they are so perfect and cute and good for each other but, on the other hand, <b>MY HEART</b>, because the reason for this comfort is painful as <b>fuck</b>.<br /><br />Sophie and Keefe are adorable, precious and perfect. They need each other. They are ALWAYS there for each other.<br /><br />What a fucking OTP. <br /><br /><br /><br /><i>(Can you tell I’ve chosen a team?)</i><br /><br />Okay, I realise I keep taking the piss out of Sophie and Fitz being pushed together for the plot, but I suppose I understand the general purpose? It’s just that her interactions with Keefe were <i>all them</i>; there were no other players obligating them to spend so much time together. Sophie and Fitz are... <i>fine</i>, but I don’t see the spark. They just don’t interest me.<br /><br />Fitz and Keefe have absolutely <b>zero</b> chemistry. I actually can’t believe they’re best friends seeing as they never even talk. Dex and Keefe are a faaar superior combination, in my not so humble opinion. It’s great when they team up. <br /><br />Tam and Linh’s relationship is amazing! Right from the get-go, I adored their twin dynamic! The edgy emo who hates everything but will literally do <i>ANYTHING</i> for his sweetheart sister. Also, I like that Tam wasn’t thrown by Sophie’s beauty or uniqueness or whatever. That alone is enough reason to respect him. No, Tam has eyes for Biana and THANK GOD FOR THAT. GOOD. FOR. THEM. Biana deserves more appreciation! She may not do anything but she’s got to have something going for her!<br /><br />And why do I love that Fitz has a thing for Linh so much? See, Fitz, who knows he’s Mr Perfect, making goo-goo eyes at a humble, genuinely insecure girl who doesn’t know she’s breathtaking? <b>I can ship that.</b><br /><br />Biana’s crush on Keefe, once again, only got literally <b>one</b> sentence of mention. Why should Sophie feel bad about growing so close to Keefe when Biana doesn’t do anything to convey her feelings for him? More so, why doesn’t Biana do ANYTHING AT ALL? Ugh. It bothers me how useless she is.<br /><br />... ...<br /><br />The casual mention of ship names like Sokeefe, Fitzphie, Dophie, etc, elicited plenty of eye-rolls from me. These kinds of things shouldn’t be acknowledged in canon material! That’s a fandom thing, Shannon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8310454747102263566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2624449077?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Tonks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Tonks" href="/user/show/90494494-lucy-tonks">Lucy Tonks</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2624449077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11988603685054949621"><i>"Never underestimate the power of the page."</i><br/><br/>I finished this book and I'm not okay. Now I have to wait two weeks until my copies of the next four books come into the mail. Please send help, I'm not sure I'm gonna make it. So far, this is my favourite book in the series. This was everything I ever wished for. <br/><br/>The plot was so well done. There were times when I was simply laughing way too hard and there were times when I felt like I wanted to cry. And god, that ending! In the last thirty pages I was</span>
  <span id="freeText11988603685054949621" style="display:none"><i>"Never underestimate the power of the page."</i><br /><br />I finished this book and I'm not okay. Now I have to wait two weeks until my copies of the next four books come into the mail. Please send help, I'm not sure I'm gonna make it. So far, this is my favourite book in the series. This was everything I ever wished for. <br /><br />The plot was so well done. There were times when I was simply laughing way too hard and there were times when I felt like I wanted to cry. And god, that ending! In the last thirty pages I was literally like that TikTok trend with "oh no", if you know it. There were so many things happening and the only thing I could do is freak out because everything was going downhill. <br /><br />My heart broke for Keefe in this book. He is my favourite character and I don't want him to suffer. He did not deserved this! I liked how Sophie was there for him during the whole book, as he was for her in the previous two books. Their relationship is so precious! One of the most precious things in this whole wide world. <br /><br /><i>"Team Foster-Keefe will always be cooler."</i><br /><br />I could have dealt with less Fitz in this book. I like the friendship between him and Sophie but nothing more, I don't want to see them together. They do not fit together, at all. They trust eachother, but there are also times when they do not have the best understanding of eachother. The best example being Fitz's reaction and how he acted towards Sophie during Exile. <br /><br />I really liked the new characters that got introduced in this book. I really liked the twins, Tam and Linh, and I found it so interesting to learn about them. By the way I loved their hair. <br /><br />It was interesting to learn more about the Black Swan. I won't lie, at the beginning I was kinda annoyed at how they did not include the kids in their plans and they just told them what to do. Yeah, they may be kids, but they've been through so many things because of the Black Swan, that they should at least be included when the plans are made. I am curious to learn other characters who are part of the Black Swan, but, at the end, I did not expect those to characters to be part of it! <br /><br />I don't know how I'll be able to wait for two weeks for the next books. I am a mess. I need the next books! I. NEED. THEM.</span>

<div id="review_1094598350" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1094598350?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Cecilia" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Cecilia" href="/user/show/22212784-cecilia"> Cecilia</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1094598350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8078229103967816989">So after finishing Everblaze I have a TON of predictions/please make it happen! <br/><br/>1. Does any one think that Master Leto is Mr. Forkle/ works with the Black Swan? Because during the boo. He says "you kids" and no other character has said that except Mr. Forkle. Also we know that Prentince was the beacon of the cold tower, couldn't they have someone in the sliver tower? Another thing is that Jolie was in the Sliver tower when she died. Lastly, master Leto a telepath and so is Mr. Forkle. And he wan</span>
  <span id="freeText8078229103967816989" style="display:none">So after finishing Everblaze I have a TON of predictions/please make it happen! <br /><br />1. Does any one think that Master Leto is Mr. Forkle/ works with the Black Swan? Because during the boo. He says "you kids" and no other character has said that except Mr. Forkle. Also we know that Prentince was the beacon of the cold tower, couldn't they have someone in the sliver tower? Another thing is that Jolie was in the Sliver tower when she died. Lastly, master Leto a telepath and so is Mr. Forkle. And he wanted Sophie not to tell the Councillers that Sophie could still use her powers with the circlet.<br /><br />2. I want to find out what special abilities Jensi and Marella get.<br /><br />3. Why is Marella so tired? I know for a fact that she was jealous of Biana, but what if she's a.... Pyrokecnic?( sorry if a spell it wrong... But FIRE USER!!!!!) but it would make sense. But maybe her paras ts are in the Black Swan and she's a spy or something?<br /><br />4. Is this quartet or a five book series? <br /><br />5. Anyway i think we all know that she'll end up with Fitz, but TEAM KEFFE!!!<br /><br />UPDATE 1/11/15<br /><br />1. We got a title a couple days ago:NEVERSEEN. Pretty mysterious don't ya think? I hope we get some more back story on the rebel group.<br /><br />UPDATE 4/17/15<br /><br />Okay it's been forever since the cover was revealed, but I do have something thoughts on it. The cover does look cool, but is still think that the Everblaze one was awesome!! So hmm. First thing I see is a big wave coming in on a stone building. Maybe they're in Atlantis? Or maybe they're using one of those forbidden stars light to jump. All of our crew is dressed up pretty fancily, maybe there's a party is some sort? And why only Keefe, Biana, and Sophie? Of they were going into any danger, Dex and Fitz would have insisted on being there. And Biana and Keefe kind-of holding hands? *arches eyebrow* Do I smell a romance? We'll they can have me blessing, but I still want Keefe for myself. </span>

<div id="review_1130660277" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130660277" />
    <a title="Mossring" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36697449-mossring"><img alt="Mossring" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490456347p2/36697449.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1130660277?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mossring" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mossring" href="/user/show/36697449-mossring">Mossring</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1130660277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5544203714690768837"><blockquote>
  <i>“The more she thought about it, the more she realised both sides had lost an important alternate perspective. And maybe that was what she'd been created for.<br/>A girl from both worlds, who'd seen the follies and triumphs of each side.<br/>And her job was to shake things up and do something new.” </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>When I finished reading <i>Neverseen</i>, all those information was too big to absorb, and I didn't like it at first--because I had no idea what had been going on. So I went and reread the book--and this time I was</span>
  <span id="freeText5544203714690768837" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“The more she thought about it, the more she realised both sides had lost an important alternate perspective. And maybe that was what she'd been created for.<br />A girl from both worlds, who'd seen the follies and triumphs of each side.<br />And her job was to shake things up and do something new.” </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />When I finished reading <i>Neverseen</i>, all those information was too big to absorb, and I didn't like it at first--because I had no idea what had been going on. So I went and reread the book--and this time I wasn't disappointed. It truly was better than Everblaze--making it the best book in the series--Shannon Messenger has outdone herself once again.<br /><br />We have our 5 heroes--Sophie, Fitz, Keefe, Dex, and Biana--setting out to join the Black Swan. There were new characters like Tam and Linh, Calla, Sior, Lur, Mitya, Blur, Squall, Wraith, Granite...etc etc. My favourite new character is now Tam. And my least favourite new character is Calla. <br /><br />I have nothing against Calla. It's just that <b>I could open any book and it would tell the almost exact same story as how Calla's ended.</b><br /><br />Also, Calla is great, but I would've wanted to see more of Sior, Lur, Mitya, and the other gnomes that represent the entire species.<br /><br />Tam and Linh were my favourite characters in this book, probably partly because they were the new characters that had the most potential of becoming main characters in the later books. I found their clashing personalities a little like yin and yang. Also, Tam's protectiveness over Linh is adorable, and the tough situations they have faced makes me want to give them a big hug. I loved the relationship between Sophie and Tam too--how Sophie tries to convince Tam that she could be trusted and she could help him and Linh. <br /><br />Sophie and Linh share a lot of similarities--they are too powerful for their own good, they're cast aside by others, and most importantly, <b>they know what it's like to be different</b>. I believe these two could really be good friends as the series progresses.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I made her a necklace one time. Did I tell you that? I made it out of beads to match her favourite bracelet. I painted a different flower on every one. And do you know how many times she wore it?"</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Overall, <b>I felt that Neverseen was more of Keefe's story rather than Sophie's</b>, even though it's told in Sophie's point of view. Sophie and Keefe had so much moments together that develops their relationship even further--to a point that both of them trust each other like how Sophie and Fitz do. Keefe takes on an angrier side in this book--and Sophie is usually the one who goes and comforts him. <br /><br />Quite a lot of people are saying that they didn't like Keefe's personality in this book, but I understood him perfectly and got why he was the way he is in <i>Neverseen</i>. This book really spoke to me on different levels and I really enjoyed reading it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5544203714690768837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1194986577?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thalia Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thalia Grace" href="/user/show/38478401-thalia-grace">Thalia Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194986577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10064867528127644387">Have you ever felt like you just want to curl up in a ball and die or just scream at the top of your lungs at anyone who approaches you? If you answered yes, then this book is right for you. <br/><br/>This book pulled at my heartstrings and kept my brain jumping around in anticipation the whole time, and even after it the book ended, because who doesn't like waiting a whole year after a cliffhanger? <br/><br/>Shannon Messenger is a goddess and devil at writing. (No offense intended.) What she has is both a gift and</span>
  <span id="freeText10064867528127644387" style="display:none">Have you ever felt like you just want to curl up in a ball and die or just scream at the top of your lungs at anyone who approaches you? If you answered yes, then this book is right for you. <br /><br />This book pulled at my heartstrings and kept my brain jumping around in anticipation the whole time, and even after it the book ended, because who doesn't like waiting a whole year after a cliffhanger? <br /><br />Shannon Messenger is a goddess and devil at writing. (No offense intended.) What she has is both a gift and a curse, and I wish that it would be spread about more in the book community, because these books definitely need more recognition.<br /><br />After book three, Everblaze, this series was on par with Harry Potter. After Neverseen, KOTLC has well surpassed it in my favorite series list. <br /><br />So while, you're reading this and you might think I'm a calm person. (Well, probably not, but just go with it.) Just know that although I may look like a calm person on the outside, on the inside I am a mess of a person trying to cope with all the feels that are currently consuming my life. <br /><br />Who cares about school or grades or work when you can shrivel down and cry while obsessing over fictional characters? (Just kidding, stay in school, you kids. (See what I did there?))<br /><br />There is so much more that I would like to discuss with you, but right now I can barely write down any coherent thoughts in my mind. Although, Shannon Messenger, if you ever happen to read this, I have a few things to say. <br /><br />Keefe.... Why..... How.... Prentice....ASDFGHJKL.... Thank you.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1296856146" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296856146" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1296856146?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481432290" href="/book/show/24885836-neverseen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=on-my-shelves">on-my-shelves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=owned-print-copy">owned-print-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296856146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7242829869319374730">In general, I don’t really believe in guilty pleasure books. I mean, how fucked up is it to feel guilty about things that are harmless and bring your pleasure. Still, I have to admit that I have them, and this series would top the list. Well, actually not even the whole series. At some point, I was most definitely one hundred percent hate reading. Then, at another point that changed. Neverseen is the point where I am completely fully embarrassed to admit that, as much as I know it’s completely t</span>
  <span id="freeText7242829869319374730" style="display:none">In general, I don’t really believe in guilty pleasure books. I mean, how fucked up is it to feel guilty about things that are harmless and bring your pleasure. Still, I have to admit that I have them, and this series would top the list. Well, actually not even the whole series. At some point, I was most definitely one hundred percent hate reading. Then, at another point that changed. Neverseen is the point where I am completely fully embarrassed to admit that, as much as I know it’s completely terrible objectively, I’m also a complete emotional wreck in the scary shipping place. This, my friends, is a guilty pleasure, so much so that I binge read in a couple of days even though I was busy and it’s unreasonably massive.<br /><br />It is really hard to be completely logical about this series because it is so absurdly ridiculously weird and silly. As Gillian said (we read it together), we would definitely have loved this to pieces if we were wee children. TBH, we love it now but also we hate ourselves for it and that’s the difference. There’s this phrase over and over in Anne Bishop’s Others series that really applies to Keeper of the Lost Cities: both wondrous and terrible. I mean, quality-wise most of it is dreck, but there are these flashes of brilliance and oh my god the feels.<br /><br />Basically, it all comes down to one character: KEEFE. Somehow, in the midst of obnoxious, flat, boring characters, Keefe was born. He’s hilarious, sarcastic, clever, and basically a lost Weasley twin who somehow ended up in this book. He’s completely unlike all the rest of Messenger’s characters in either series (though the YA one does have a pale imitation). Keefe makes everyone and everything better. Like, you know how Major Lilywhite on iZombie is boring as fuck but then the moment he hangs out with Ravi he’s totally okay? Keefe is like that. Every single character is improved by Keefe being nearby, most especially Sophie. But even Dex is tolerable in this book because he and Keefe bond together to make fun of Fitzphie and basically Keefe is the best ever.<br /><br />What is not the best ever is stuff like the plot. The five kids (Sophie, Keefe, Fitz, Biana, and Dex) have been expelled from their fancy elf school so they run off to Black Swan to avoid punishment by the Council for their shenanigans in book three. Black Swan is like “okay, kids, you need to study for a couple of weeks and then we’ll take you on a mission” and the kids are like “WHAT DO YOU MEAN STUDY MISSIONS NOW.” Meanwhile, I’m like “um, you’re five, so you should go on no missions.” Like, I actually totally support the studying and safety plan for the children which basically means I’m a boring adult now.<br /><br />However, these adults are total idiots. Fitz and Biana’s mom and the leaders of the Black Swan Collective agree to the dumbest shit. Their actual plan for the mission is just the worst. Literally, they’re like “kids, you do all the work. We’ll come along for moral support and to be the distraction so you can escape if things go wrong, which we’ll do by wiping our memories and thus leaving the movement for good we are leading. And for some reason all four of us need to go because reasons.” Is it any wonder the forces of evil are winning? Absolutely not, given how good these guys are at noticing suspicious behavior that is foreshadowed with all the subtlety of a hammer to the eyeball.<br /><br />Then there are the kids’ plans which tbh are slightly better but still terrible. When the kids tell the adults, the adults are like “oh okay, yeah, why don’t you do that? but we couldn’t let you go into enemy territory alone!” At which point you’re all “YES DO NOT LET THEM.” And then the adults are like “make sure you take these two children who are not part of our organization with you.” Like, how the hell is Della not stopping this shit or at least going along to protect them? The adults in this series could not be more useless, I swear. I mean, they didn’t even hug Keefe.<br /><br />Then there’s the straight up whacked out nonsense, like how all of these young teens have stuffed animals with cutesy names they cannot bear to be without. Or the fact that Biana randomly adopts Iggy in the middle for no reason. Why is Iggy even still here? But anyway. How about the scene where one of the members of Black Swan basically disguises himself as Grover from Sesame Street? Or the fact that another one is disguised as The Thing from Fantastic 4 and goes by Granite? The weirdest shit though was the two plus pages about alicorn sex. I am not making this shit up, I swear.<br /><br />The plot and world building is like .5 stars but the feels are like a million stars, and I just refuse to rate this higher than three stars but my god I was mess reading this book. Shannon Messenger is SO FUCKING MEAN to Keefe in this book. I cannot even. No one else really has character development but Keefe’s arc is so well done albeit cruelly. I really do not get how he appeared in this book and is such perfection at all times.<br /><br />I do not have the ability to explain the amount that I am invested in this ship and this character and the amount that I was completely wrecked by the events of this book. Sophie and Keefe are so perfect and clearly IN LOVE but she doesn’t know and Shannon Messenger spends the WHOLE BOOK taunting both Fitzphie and Team Foster Keefe shippers, but come on Sophie and Keefe hold hands like three million times SURELY IT MUST BE CANON. But also I do not trust Messenger to make the right choices with the romance here and I am fucking terrified of book five for so many reasons.<br /><br />I preordered this book in hardcover and paid actual money for it and I’m going to do the same with book five. This has been an exercise in self-loathing, desperation, and the scary place. You should all join me here because <s>misery really loves company</s> it’s great.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7242829869319374730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1048685550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1048685550" />
    <a title="Mariam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31657573-mariam"><img alt="Mariam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601068489p2/31657573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1048685550?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariam" href="/user/show/31657573-mariam">Mariam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=2015-publication">2015-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1048685550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8996788216648593787">Reread: 1/3/18<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Is it okay if I enter your mind?”<br/>“Dude, do you realize how creepy that sounds?”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><i>Neverseen</i> continues to follow the same pattern as the rest of the KOTLC series- a slow beginning, a boring (but slowly improving) Sophie, character development, and....a cliffhanger!<br/><br/>Other species other than the elves finally begin to play a bigger role in the book which is exciting! Woohoo! I'm not too happy with the addition of the new characters, Tam and Linh, though. Just when I thought Messenger</span>
  <span id="freeText8996788216648593787" style="display:none">Reread: 1/3/18<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Is it okay if I enter your mind?”<br />“Dude, do you realize how creepy that sounds?”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><i>Neverseen</i> continues to follow the same pattern as the rest of the KOTLC series- a slow beginning, a boring (but slowly improving) Sophie, character development, and....a cliffhanger!<br /><br />Other species other than the elves finally begin to play a bigger role in the book which is exciting! Woohoo! I'm not too happy with the addition of the new characters, Tam and Linh, though. Just when I thought Messenger was beginning to add personality to her originals', <i>they</i> show up. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>Together they looked like K-pop idols, or like they’d stepped straight out of anime.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Tam resembles the "dark and mysterious" anime persona and Linh is literally Juvia Lockser from the anime <i>Fairy Tail</i> Don't believe me?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Water pleads for my attention. But too often it’s a trick.” As she spoke, the mist thickened into a storm that soaked them with a heavy downpour.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Juvia much?<br /><br /> One of my favorite parts of the series (something I hadn't realized until now) is Messenger's way of saying "the world isn't black and white." Unlike other novels such as <i>Hunger Games</i>, <i>Divergent</i>, and <i>Red Queen</i>, Messenger doesn't create a plot with only a "corrupt government" and "ordinary" people trying to create rebellion. She shows how all the groups: the Councillors, the Neverseen, and the Black Swan, have right and wrong ideas. <br /><br />Now, since the love-triangle (sorry, Dex) between Sophie, Keefe, and Fitz seems to have escalated, I'm going to go on a little tangent and write about why I ship Sophitz.<br /><br />Before I begin, I'd like to say there's a fifty percent chance the Sophitz ship will sail and fifty percent chance the Sokeefe ship will sail. Yes, I think Keefe and Sophie has as much of a chance of getting together as Sophie and Fitz- so I'm not disregarding you, Sokeefe fans. But here's why (just one reason!) I think Sokeefe cannot happen- <i>as of now.</i><br /><br />Keefe needs to learn to love and trust himself first. It's true- Sophie's friendship and trust in him helps, but he needs to push aside his guilt before he is able to create a future with Sophie. How do I know Keefe doesn't trust himself? Because he's constantly asking Sophie if she trusts him. While Fitz and Dex do the same, it's more to reinforce whatever they're arguing, while with Keefe, it's not. Until then, Sokeefe can't happen.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Team Foster-Keefe will always be cooler.” <br />“Yeah, but Sophitz will be unstoppable,” Fitz said.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Fitz may seem like a perfect character with his "movie-star grin," but beside his smile, there's nothing perfect about him. He makes mistakes like any other character, as seen in <i>Exile</i> and several other times throughout the series. <b>Lacking a miserable past does not make you a perfect person.</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“In your case, Fitz—while you’re an incredibly talented Telepath—your skills simply do not match Sophie’s.” <br />Sophie cringed, wondering if the criticism would bother Fitz. But he grinned at her and said, “Yeah, she makes us all look bad.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Sophitz may seem "perfect" superficially, but I find it quite unique in comparison to typical YA and MG relationships. In the beginning of the series, twelve-year-old Sophie had a crush on Fitz.<br /><br />Understandable.<br /><br />Yet...why does fourteen-year-old Sophie <i>still</i> have a "crush" on Fitz? Though only two years have passed, the mental and physical development between the age groups is very different. It could be that the crush is simply a crush. I think it's turned into something more. What makes this even better is that Fitz showed no interest in Sophie before, even going as far as referring to her as his younger sister.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>The brightness in Fitz’s mind dimmed, and the pattern seemed to melt into a swamp of murky gray green. <br />“Disappointment?” she tried. <br />“Now it is,” Keefe said. “Before it was jealousy.” <br />“Jealousy over what?” Sophie asked. <br />“Is it my turn to guess?” Fitz said, changing the subject.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />He likes her. She likes him. So what's the problem? <br /><br />THEY'RE OBLIVIOUS. COME ON, GUYS! EVEN KEEFE KNOWS!<br /><br />#SophitzWillSail<br />#IWillNotLetAnotherShipSink (aka <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17167166.Crown_of_Midnight__Throne_of_Glass___2_" title="Crown of Midnight (Throne of Glass, #2) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Crown of Midnight</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8996788216648593787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1847000741730922315">Neverseen...<br/>Juicy, full of excitement, riveting, Not a bland moment, full of suspense and action, everything you'll want in a fantasy book.<br/>This was a fabulous, thrilling fourth sequel to the Keeper of The Lost Cities series. It spiced up a bit when they were describing Lady Gisela's maybe-so death. AND EVERYTHING CHANGED when Alvar was unmasked as the "Boy Who Disappeared" THINGS CHANGED EVEN MORE when Keefe went to the Neutral Territories to join the Neverseen. I was heartbroken!! I have shelte</span>
  <span id="freeText1847000741730922315" style="display:none">Neverseen...<br />Juicy, full of excitement, riveting, Not a bland moment, full of suspense and action, everything you'll want in a fantasy book.<br />This was a fabulous, thrilling fourth sequel to the Keeper of The Lost Cities series. It spiced up a bit when they were describing Lady Gisela's maybe-so death. AND EVERYTHING CHANGED when Alvar was unmasked as the "Boy Who Disappeared" THINGS CHANGED EVEN MORE when Keefe went to the Neutral Territories to join the Neverseen. I was heartbroken!! I have sheltered a crush on Keefe since half of the first book. I mean, I was heartbroken, but it didn't make the book one jot less wonderful. Shannon wrote this novel beautifully, with twists and turns, ups and downs, fears and joy. The plot was weaved intricately, with each little tiny event being a little thread inside of the big web. I WOULD HIGHLY RECOMMEND THIS TO ANYBODY becasue it's marked Juvenile, and because it's a sure-to-love novel that will keep the pages flipping.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1847000741730922315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10715513546644164172" style="display:none">*heart eyes* <br /><br />Wowowow. Just like all of the others in this series, I LOVED this book!!! <br /><br />Content/Language- No cuss words that I caught. If I missed anything, please correct me. <br />*A bird's name is quite embarrassing/innapropriate. Since I borrowed this from a friend, they were sweet enough to black out this bird's name.* <br />*The allicorns in this book are mating and Silveny gets pregnant. Not very descriptive, but sensitive readers beware! Again, this was blacked out in the book I borrowed. Thank you, friend! *fist bump** <br />Mentions of some characters cursing under their breath. They did not actually say any curse words!!! There are some crude jokes. <br /><br />Violence- There are several fight scenes. For readers who are extra sensitive about this, this may not be the series for you! There are several fight scenes per book. <br /><br />Romance- Crushes, hand-holding, laying heads on shoulders, hugs, etc. There is no kissing. Clean! <br /><br />Need I say it again? I LOVE THIS SERIES❤ The world-building, character developement, EVERYTHING IS INCREDIBLE!!! There are so many plot twists, that you don't think that they will all come together. But they all do! The endings are so happy, but leave just enough of a cliff-hanger for you to NEED MORE!!! <br /><br />Keefe... oh Keefe... WHY?!? ❤ <br /><br />I loved that we learned so much about both the Black Swan and the Neverseen in this book! Tam and Linh are such a nice touch as well. <br /><br />Anyhoo... I need the next book pronto, and as always a five star rating from me. <br /><br />Thank you so much, Ms. Messenger, for writing this series. Your writing is INCREDIBLE!!!<br /><br />I'm starting to love Keefe... but Fitz😍 Still #Team Fitz:))</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2158185805" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2158185805" />
    <a title="Maddie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60336580-maddie"><img alt="Maddie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498658110p2/60336580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2158185805?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie" href="/user/show/60336580-maddie">Maddie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2158185805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4841684304194442750">2.5/3<br/><br/>My complaints about the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2073956074' rel='nofollow noopener'>previous book, Everblaze,</a> are unfortunately still relevant to Neverseen. <br/><br/>Each book in this series is both a major step forward and major step backward. There were elements of this book that I felt were quite strong, mostly the development of Keefe's character and the additions of Tam and Linh. There were a few actions sequences at the end of the book that I felt were well done and showed that this series can be enjoyable when the characters' abilities have concrete l</span>
  <span id="freeText4841684304194442750" style="display:none">2.5/3<br /><br />My complaints about the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2073956074" rel="nofollow noopener">previous book, Everblaze,</a> are unfortunately still relevant to Neverseen. <br /><br />Each book in this series is both a major step forward and major step backward. There were elements of this book that I felt were quite strong, mostly the development of Keefe's character and the additions of Tam and Linh. There were a few actions sequences at the end of the book that I felt were well done and showed that this series can be enjoyable when the characters' abilities have concrete limits and are used sparingly/with everyone working together and contributing. I also felt the final few chapters were very compelling and reminded me why I have continued with this series. When it's good, it's good. <br /><br />Like I said in my review of the previous book, the motivations of the various factions in the series are not outlined clearly. I think this was a mistake, because (a) this is book FOUR, (b) there were several moments where it seemed like the Black Swan and the Neverseen had the same motivations, and (c) because the factions don't have clear-cut goals, histories, and motivations, it makes it difficult to understand the motivations of the characters working for them. And your characters need to have motivations. A big part of the reason that Keefe and Tam are interesting, well-defined, and compelling characters is because they have explicit motivations and goals. <br /><br />Relatedly, I find the callous and superior attitude some of the characters (who are supposed to be the good guys) have towards humans really bizarre and not in alignment with some of what we are told about the Black Swan in earlier books. It seems doubly weird because Sophie spent the majority of her life in the human world. There is a scene where Mr. Frokle is talking about his days moonlighting as a fertility doctor and how he met hundreds of (human) women who struggled to get pregnant, and how he could have “fixed all of them”. Like, come on….do we have to go down this road? In a middle-grade book? For <i>human</i> readers? And of course there's the added implication that not being able to get pregnant means you're broken. I think this line perfectly encapsulates everything wrong with this series: there was so little <i>thought</i> put into so much of it. But how does a writer not put thought into things? Isn't the entire conceit of writing that words mean things and have implications?<br /><br />I also found the first half of the book a real struggle to get through, and both the juvenile/anachronistic language much more grating in this book than in the previous ones. By 'juvenile', I don't really mean language and jokes that kids in this book's age demographic would find funny, because I don't have a right to be upset about those. It's more that the anachronisms were juvenile. Good examples would be Sophie using the word fangirl and all the ship names. I thought the joke about Sophie and Keefe being "Team Foster-Keefe" that was coined in the second book was acceptable as they spent the majority of that book hanging out together and hyphenating their names wasn't a direct reference to ship names, but more of a subtle nod. I also thought it was a clever way to show that Keefe's issues with his family were extensive enough that he didn't want to be referred to by his last name. But the conventional ship naming in this book were just too over the top and continually drew me out of the story because that entire practice isn't elvin, it's human. <br /><br />Overall: I'm (but kind of begrudgingly) continuing with the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4841684304194442750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tmaLMYAUxrkQOFVA9i7DdbODaE55xDQWbaWTYLiMGTfVkC7OQeJyLXEgjg1ToXsZy9ImWinR3lAqPlNneqzOug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dFu0TCm6kYIphjLhadEcowudMozitQFauvm21XwFte4XrRGz6EwlFkie6azMXqTPc8x8mLKg6xz9YnbSviViYw==')})
  }
//]]>
